1532214789843<//Date>
< text>
Great place to camp, backpack, or just day hike. Only a short hike to the top, but just make sure you follow the trail to the top! The first time I went, I continued on straight and accidentally missed the trail to the top of Mount Pinos. Just make sure to keep left upon leaving the first bit of trail past the trailhead. Great views, cool weather to beat the heat. Highly recommend this weekend getaway!

Also, you can continue on past the top of Mount Pinos (the highest point in Kern County) And hike to the neighboring Sawmill Mountain (the highest point in Ventura County). A great hike!</text>

<review>I work in the mall and have eaten as this location several times. It's the perfect spot for a burger if you want higher quality than McDonald's but cheaper than Buckhorn. I've worked in food service and know how difficult it is to iron out the initial kinks and get things off the ground. With this location being brand new to the area, they are often slammed with in person and mobile orders, as well as delivery courier orders. But every time I'm there while it's overwhelmingly busy I see how hard the employees are working to do the best the can, the fastest they can.

My overall review lost a star simply because special orders often get overlooked. I usually add vegetables to my Smoke Shack burger and I love getting the chocolate/vanilla shake- but almost every time I'm given just a chocolate shake and often the vegetables are left off. Not a huge deal as there is no up charge for adding on extras. But it would still be nice to get what I order. If I'm observing correctly it looks like some of the shakes are pre made, presumably to save time- but full transparency goes a long way with customers. If there's no time to give me the chocolate/vanilla option, just let me know!

Overall, besides the obvious hiccups that come with a brand new store, I  am happy to continue eating here!  Hoping they continue to grow and fall into a consistent rhythm. I have high hopes! They seem to hire hard workers, and a location is only as good as it's employees.<//review><gmapID>0x809b21bdb3088835:0x6aa48a4b1336637d</gmapID><user_name>Valor and Kaitlyn Nash<//user_name><Pics>None</Pics>< resp>

The unfortunate thing is that the food was amazing....
It was unfortunate because we received (only 3 burgers) from our total order which was (4 burgers, 1 grill cheese, 2 fries, 1 cheese fries, 10 piece chicken bites), and you might say its an honest mistake? The problem we have though is not that our food was missing, but more so there was NO solutions to help us with the mistake... Shake Shack has NO real-time way for a customer to contact a manager for help (Their phone number refers you to their website OR you can leave a voicemail) and it says a manager will call you back within 24hrs???  I just left a voicemail with my number but not expecting anything to come from it, honestly, theres little value in a call back "tomorrow" about our order error "tonight". Anyhow, we ordered dinner elsewhere, only leaving feedback because the food at Shake Shake was amazing, it'd be a real shame to have food THAT GREAT yet lose customers due to terrible process/customer service solutions.   Wish you the best.<//review>

Long wait for below average food. This was definitely not worth the wait. My Shack burger tasted like a Wendy’s cheeseburger. We also got a spicy chicken sandwich. Guess what that tasted like? Chick-Fil-A! The only thing that resembled other Shake Shacks was the mushroom burger my wife ordered. So disappointing.

We ordered 5 items and 2 were wrong. We ordered cheese fries but they came out with no cheese. We also ordered a Diet Coke but we got a Cherry Coke instead. What the!?! How hard is it to assemble fast food?

We love the Shake Shack in Las Vegas and we were so excited when one opened up here in Roseville but sadly it’s just not the same.

I’d eat here again but definitely wouldn’t go out of my way for it.

A solid 2/5!</review>

< review>
I am a great supporter of small businesses. I love this ethnic market. Great & personable. It is well located in the heart of Berkeley & close to the freeway 80. There are some things that I can usually only find in this market.

Specialties:

Olives, Turkish Honey with 10 different kinds of nuts ( good for an oat meal), organic raw honey from Brazil, lentils, frozen kebabs and breads, variety of yogurts & Cheese, great prices on olive oil, meat counter offers great prices on meat & so much more. Meat is fresh, organic and clean. Meat Counter does not smell at all. It is a small but very clean store with variety. Not a lot of produce but what they had looked good and prices were nice. They should start carrying fresh produce.

I highly recommend it. Folks are very friendly and polite, Inshahallah:)<//review>

<name>Joy<//name><Date>1600844423129< /Date>< Rating>
3< /Rating>
< Review>
It seems the dining situation has been picking up, the outdoor dining situation at least. Every weekend, it looks like Gott's has a sizable amount of people seated in front of the Ferry Building. When outdoor dining first reopened, I was hesitant about stepping into a restaurant again, regardless of breathing in open air. So I waited for other patrons to be our guinea pigs before joining in. So far, so good, or at least not terrible...
I've never eaten at Gott's before, but I have had the Strauss soft serve, which is always good on a hot day, no complaints there.

Like all other establishments, the queue has circles placed on the ground, positioned 6 feet apart. You order at the register and take a beeper to your table. When it beeps, you take it to the food pickup station.

$10.99 Bacon Cheeseburger - American cheese, Zoe's bacon, lettuce, tomatoes, pickles, secret sauce on toasted egg bun:
For this area, this is a reasonably priced burger and cooked well. It was a nice medium rare patty with a good bun to patty ratio, and had cheese melted over the patty. So important. Also, the lettuce, tomatoes, and pickles tasted fresh and crisp, and the bun was fluffy.

$3.99 Garlic Fries in garlic butter & parsley:
Mr. Joy, the fry connoisseur deemed them tasty enough to polish off.

$13.99 Baja Fish Tacos - fresh mahi mahi, beer-battered & fried, in soft, organic corn tortillas with Mexican slaw, cilantro, salsa verde, lime, spicy mayo:
I was aiming for something light, but these tacos were pretty big. The mahi mahi is generously portioned, the batter not too heavy, and the tart salsa verde helped cut through the fried batter.

I appreciate that the larger tables have benches with high backs to add separation from other patrons. Also, their waste situation is commendable, as they only have compost and recycling bins. All other items are reusable or washable.

Overall, the food selection is pretty typical of what you'd find from American cuisine, or from diners. Nothing out of the ordinary. I'd give the food a 7/10, and the service was on par too.
One thing about ordering that could be improved - there are no menus at the register, so you need to know what you want before it is your turn to order. The enlarged menus are posted outside of the ordering queue.
When we visited, the wait in line wasn't too bad. I'd still say this is a nice place to have a snack or relaxed meal as long as the wait isn't too long.< /Review>

< Text>
I was told that this place was amazeballs and that I had to try it out. The "best burgers" in the city they said. I'll be the judge of that I said.

First a little bio. I've tried several burger joints in many different districts in this city, be it a chain, mom and pops or fast food giant.

Being in somewhat a tourist area, I was skeptic on trying the place out, but my former coworker and I decided to try it out for lunch since we wanted to try something new. I got a plain old cheeseburger just to put my feet in the water, with some fries and a side of ranch.

It's 1pm on a Tuesday, so the lunch rush has died down so we were able to order our food and start grubbin in 20 minutes. I had mixed feelings with the cheeseburger like something was missing(like I should've gotten the California burger) I was more in love with the fries with ranch which is pretty much what saved my meal. In a way the burger reminded me of Shake Shack in New York, probably due to the soft buns.

I would probably give this place another chance and try out the California burger next time and might get better results, but really the fries with ranch alone is enough to pull me back here. You know, maybe it's not even the fries, maybe it's just the ranch. That ranch is what's amazeballs here. Yeah it must be it.  Make sure you try dem ranch on everything if you decide to come here. They're amazeballs.<//Text>

<Rate>4< /Rate><review>OK, so I've been here a couple times in the last year and can add some marginally better than random info:
- Impossible Burger v2.0, as featured this week in the Chronicle: I'm gonna say it was measurably better than the previous version.  As in, this is the first time I've not been 100% sure it didn't contain meat... it's definitely not 100% meat, but I wouldn't swear it was "meat free" if I had tasted it blind.   Now as for appearance, the Impossible patty on the Impossible cheeseburger I had Saturday night looked a bit more like a "commodity freezer burger shaped puck" than the previous versions I remember having, which had more of a "freshly ground" look to it.  But we're going for taste not appearance here.  And freezer burger meat is burger meat.
- Ambiguous tip of the week: on a previous visit here, I ordered something (the Ahi burger or poke tacos I think) that was a "Yelp highlight" and it vastly exceeded expectations.  No it doesn't sound like something a burger place would be great at and yes it was.  So risk it.

The fries were just meh.  Too much potato flavor!</review>< Date>

Think of Gott's as an elevated Foster's Freeze with artisan burgers and soft serve! You can order your burger with grilled onions for free. The fries are in a good sized portion and don’t forget to ask for their special dipping sauces. I haven’t tried their salads or ahi creations but plan on doing so soon. Soft serve is a pricey at $4 for a small, but you can get two flavors, tastes delicious and overall worth the splurge. Also makes for great shakes. Order ahead online to avoid the line and get your food at the pick up counter.< /Review>

< Review>
Gott's is famous for their burgers and that is exactly what you should order here.  They make a great burger and fries.  It is a bit of a chain with a few other locations but the Ferry Building is nice with a large outdoor patio on the Embarcadero and typically fast service.  It is a no-thrills kind of place; a fairly typical old school burger joint.  But the food is good, and the service is quick if you are looking for a decent burger.< /Review>

A deliciously casual restaurant with outdoor seating reminiscent of a beer garden.  Great for groups because you order at the front and then are seated and served.  Great selection of beers, burgers, and my personal favorite the fried chicken breakfast sandwich (the most delicious heart attack you will ever eat!).  I also recommend the ahi tacos, garlic french fries, and the mint milkshake.
It does get very busy during the weekday lunch rush but turnover is quick!

Just hankering for something sweet, they also sell soft serve on the inside of the building without the line.< /review>

If you are wandering around the Embarcadero near the Ferry Building and are looking for a bite to eat, Gott's may be a good option. It's mainly about burgers and fries and stuff that goes with burgers and fries (salads, beer, shakes, ...). They have a lot of burger options and even have a pretty good veggie patty. They have both indoor and outdoor seating, mostly at long, shared tables. The line to order can get pretty long during the lunch rush, but it's pretty good if you have the time.< /text>

< review>
Their ahi burger was on 7x7's list of things to eat in San Francisco.  So naturally, I had to try it.  It was pricey, around $14, but it was really delicious and filling! I'm glad I didn't order fries.  On another occasion when I went here with my cousins, I ordered the ahi tacos and sweet potato fries.  My cousins ordered garlic fries and chili cheese fries, and had their own hamburgers.  It was a feast!

The atmosphere is like a diner, and the long tables are great for big groups.  The line gets very long at peak times since it's located in the Ferry Building.  But if you want a good hamburger in the area, Gott's is the place to go.<//review>

<Pics>None</Pics><response>None</response><text>Fast and convenient, but food's not great. Very greasy and overly salty. It's mediocre pub food. One of the cheaper places to have a meal in the ferry building. Meh...< /text></record></dataset><record>
<response>None</response><username>Yvette Tung< /username><gmap_id>0x808580668c955555:0x3f07d5248c09fe1f< /gmap_id>< userid>
104581666364747365732<//userid>
<date>1448482136663</date><rating>4<//rating>< Pics>
None</Pics>
< Text>
Legit burgers for those who are seeking something other than seafood near the Embarcadero. Most are served on TOASTED EGG BUNS!

Men seem to love the Western Bacon Blue Ring Burger (onion rings + blue cheese with bbq sauce). It's exactly what I would expect a mouthful of American to taste like. Still looking for seafood? Try the Ahi Burger, whose thick chunk of lightly-seared tuna blends perfectly with the ginger wasabi mayo sauce. My favorite.

Quite possibly the only place in the world where I'd skip on the chili cheese fries. Luckily they have delicious garlic* fries and sweet potato fries for fry-addicts.

Thumbs up for using compostable packaging, but why not reusable materials? Still, A for effort.

*garlic makes the world go 'round</Text>
